Or maybe he made himself part<sup class="footnote-marker">69</sup><i class="footnote">הקנה is short for הִקְנָה שְׁבִיתָתוֹ “intended to acquire his Sabbath resting place at …”</i> of his town when it was still daytime? It was found stated: In the morning the sun shone. They told him, rabbi, here the town is before you, please enter<sup class="footnote-marker">70</sup><i class="footnote">He really was on a trip, slept outside and realized where he was in the morning. R. Jehudah might read שֶׁיָּשַׁן also in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Eruvin 4:4:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Eruvin.4.4.1">Mishnah 4</a>. The objections stated before are raised in the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Eruvin 45a" href="/Eruvin.45a">Babli 45a</a> about this <i>baraita</i>.</i>.

Halakhah 5

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> If somebody slept on the road and did not realize that night fell he has 2’000 cubits in every direction, the words of Rebbi Joḥanan ben Nuri, but the Sages say, he only has four cubits<sup class="footnote-marker">13</sup><i class="footnote">Everybody agrees that if he slept in a town during nightfall, his Sabbath domain is that of the town. But if he is outside of town, R. Joḥanan ben Nuri holds that he automatically has a Sabbath domain of 2’000 cubits in every direction but the Sages hold that a Sabbath domain can be acquired only by conscious selection. If he slept at sundown, he made no selection and has no domain. In the interpretation of the Yerushalmi, R. Jehudah agrees with R. Joḥanan ben Nuri but specifies that he may choose the center of his Sabbath domain at will and, therefore, walk 4’000 cubits in one direction (which must be chosen at the start and cannot be changed.)</i>. Rebbi Eleazar says, he is in the center; Rebbi Jehudah says, in any direction which he chooses. Rebbi Jehudah agrees that if he selected one he cannot retract it.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> Paragraph. “If somebody slept on the road and did not realize until after night fell,” etc. Rebbi Zeˋira in the name of Rebbi Ḥasdai. The reason of Rebbi Joḥanan ben Nuri: Since if he had been awake he would have acquired a Sabbath domain, when he was sleeping he did not acquire a Sabbath domain; he only has 2’000 cubits in every direction. Rebbi Jehudah says, even awake and he did not acquire a Sabbath domain; he only has 2’000 cubits in every direction<sup class="footnote-marker">71</sup><i class="footnote">As explained in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Eruvin 4:7:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Eruvin.4.7.1">Mishnah 9</a>, a Sabbath domain is a rectangular domain (for a single person a square) oriented exactly NS-EW. In a village or town, the geography of the place automatically defines the domain as explained in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Eruvin 5:1:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Eruvin.5.1.1">Mishnah 5:1</a>. For a single person the domain can be determined only by a conscious choice. In the absence of such a choice the Sabbath region is a circle, for the Sages of diameter 8 cubits, for RR. Joḥanan ben Nuri and Jehudah (possibly also R. Eliezer) 2’000 cubits. For RR. Joḥanan ben Nuri and Eliezer the place of the person at sundown automatically is the center of the circle, for R. Jehudah the person may choose any point accessible to him when he awakes as center of his circle.</i>. Rebbi Jehudah’s statement follows Rebbi Joḥanan ben Nuri’s (and exceeds Rebbi Joḥanan ben Nuri’s)<sup class="footnote-marker">72</sup><i class="footnote">The text in parentheses was written by the scribe of L but (wrongly) deleted by the corrector who it seems understood רובא as name of a person whom he could not identify. Note by S. Liebermann.</i>. For Rebbi Joḥanan ben Nuri said, since if he had been awake he would have acquired a Sabbath domain, if he was awake and did not acquire a Sabbath domain; he only has 2’000 cubits in every direction<sup class="footnote-marker">73</sup><i class="footnote">The text is elliptic; missing is a statement that for R. Jehudah the person may choose to have his Sabbath circle so that he is at the border, not at the center, and therefore has 4’000 cubits in one direction, 0 cubits in the directions perpendicular and opposite to the chosen one.</i>.
Rebbi Ḥuna said, Rav Naḥman bar Jacob asked: if a proselyte immersed himself after sunrise. “Since if he had been awake he would have acquired a Sabbath domain,” what does Rebbi Joḥanan ben Nuri say in this case? Let us hear from the following.<sup class="footnote-marker">74</sup><i class="footnote">Obviously there is a lacuna here, it is not said how to decide the question. A proselyte becomes Jewish by immersion in a <i>miqweh</i> for the purpose of conversion (for a male, after circumcision), attested to by a competent court. The latter condition excludes conversion on a Sabbath, a fact which Rav Naḥman bar Jacob, chief judge of the Exilarch’s court in Babylonia, must have known. The problem here is not about a proselyte but a general question about the Sabbath domain for a person who on Friday evening was unable or unqualified to choose a Sabbath domain; for example an insane person who became lucid overnight. Since R. Joḥanan ben Nuri restricts his argument to persons who on Friday evening were able to exercise judgment, it is unknown what his opinion would have been in this case.</i> For Rebbi Isaac bar Naḥman<sup class="footnote-marker">75</sup><i class="footnote">Read: R. Naḥman bar Isaac; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Eruvin 1:1:3" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Eruvin.1.1.3">Chapter 1, Note 62</a>.</i> said in the name of Rebbi Joshua ben Levi, practice follows Rebbi Joḥanan ben Nuri. If he selected while it still was daytime, he may change his mind while it still is daytime; after nightfall he may change his mind after nightfall<sup class="footnote-marker">76</sup><i class="footnote">This question is possible only for R. Jehudah who permits the person to choose his Sabbath area on the Sabbath as long as it is a circle of radius 2’000 and contains the point at which he stands. For all others the area is uniquely determined at nightfall.</i>. If he selected while it still was daytime, and the day became holy for him<sup class="footnote-marker">77</sup><i class="footnote">Cf. similar questions <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shabbat 3:1:13" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shabbat.3.1.13"><i>Šabbat</i> 3, Note 55</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Eruvin 4:4:2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Eruvin.4.4.2">Chapter 4, Note 70</a>.</i>? Let us hear from the following: “he may not enter, the words of Rebbi Meïr<sup class="footnote-marker">11</sup><i class="footnote">He may not go more than 2’000 cubits from the place where he started the Sabbath. Since he did not intend to be like a town dweller for this Sabbath, for him the entire built-up area is not counted as 4 cubits.</i>; Rebbi Jehudah says, he may enter<sup class="footnote-marker">78</sup><i class="footnote">Since he went to sleep outside of town and R. Jehudah allows him to change his mind in the morning and to enter town, how can the Mishnah state that R. Jehudah agrees that if he chose once he cannot change his mind?</i>” Not on this was it said, but on the start of the Chapter; on “if somebody was taken out by Gentiles or an evil spirit,” it was said . Rebbi Abun said, “Rebbi Jehudah agrees that if he selected one he cannot retract it.<sup class="footnote-marker">79</sup><i class="footnote">The question raised in the preceding Note is answered; R. Jehudah agrees that the person forcibly removed from his Sabbath domain has only one possibility of choice once he regains his freedom of choice. (R. Ḥananel <i>ad</i> 48a, <i>Sefer Haˋittim</i> p. 68 Note 152.)</i>”

Halakhah 6

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> If they were two<sup class="footnote-marker">14</sup><i class="footnote">Two people staying on the road over the Sabbath and both sleeping during twilight.</i> and some of the cubits of one were inside the cubits of the other they bring and eat in the middle on condition that one not transfer into the other’s [domain]. If they were three and the middle one absorbed between them, he is permitted with them and they with him but the two outside ones are forbidden one with the other.<br>Rebbi Simeon says, to what is this similar? To three courtyards open to one another and open to the public domain<sup class="footnote-marker">15</sup><i class="footnote">The three courtyards are in one row, and each one has a separate exit to the road. If one of the courtyards had no direct exit to the road it would be an appendix of an other courtyard and forced to have an <i>eruv</i> with the latter. But in the case here the <i>eruvim</i> are voluntary. Since the Yerushalmi does not comment on this Mishnah it must assume that this is practice, against the Babli which states that the majority disagrees with R. Simeon.</i>. If both [outer ones] made an <i>eruv</i> with the middle one, that one is permitted with them and they with it but the two outside ones are forbidden one with the other.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> Paragraph. “If they were two, and some of the cubits of one,” etc. Even though Rebbi Ḥananiah ben Antigonos disagrees with the rabbis about the cubits he agrees with them here about the environs of towns<sup class="footnote-marker">80</sup><i class="footnote">While the quote is from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Eruvin 4:6:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Eruvin.4.6.1">Mishnah 6</a>, the reference is to <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Eruvin 4:7:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Eruvin.4.7.1">Mishnah 9</a> but its original place must have been in the discussion of <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Eruvin 5:1:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Eruvin.5.1.1">Mishnah 5:1</a>, which is referred to as “here”. Only for a single person does R. Ḥanina ben Antigonos define a Sabbath domain as circular; for villages and towns he agrees that it is rectangular.</i>.

Halakhah 7

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> If somebody was on the road and afraid lest it get dark<sup class="footnote-marker">16</sup><i class="footnote">Before he can reach the next town.</i> but he knew of a tree or a wall and says, “my Sabbath rest shall be under it,” he did not say anything<sup class="footnote-marker">17</sup><i class="footnote">The place must be defined to within 4 cubits to be valid.</i>. “My Sabbath rest in its roots”, he walks from the place of his feet to the roots 2’000 cubits and from the roots to his house 2’000 cubits; it turns out that he may walk 4’000 cubits after nightfall.<br>If he does not know or is not conversant with practice and said, my Sabbath rest shall be at my place, his place empowers him 2’000 cubits in every direction, circular according to Rebbi Ḥanania ben Antigonos. But the Sages say square like a square table, that he gain the corners<sup class="footnote-marker">18</sup><i class="footnote">In the first opinion the Sabbath domain is a circular disk of radius 2’000 cubits. In the second, authoritative, opinion it is a square of side length 4’000 cubits oriented strictly NS-EW. From the center along the diagonals in fact one may walk 2’000 √2 = 2828 cubits. Most importantly, this definition also applies to Sabbath domains of towns which always are rectangular domains oriented strictly NS-EW.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> If one recognized and one did not recognize; the one who recognized may go with the one who did not recognize and the one who did not recognize may go with the one who recognized<sup class="footnote-marker">81</sup><i class="footnote">This refers to <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Eruvin 4:7:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Eruvin.4.7.1">Mishnah 8</a>, where a traveller who remembers a landmark between his situation at sundown and the next village may declare this landmark as his Sabbath center. A stranger who walks with him may adopt the other’s Sabbath center without knowing the geography. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Eruvin 50b" href="/Eruvin.50b">Babli 50b</a>.</i>.

Halakhah 8

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> That is what they said, the poor person makes an <i>eruv</i> with his feet. Rebbi Meïr says, we only have the poor. Rebbi Jehudah says, both poor and rich; they said that one makes an <i>eruv</i> with bread, only to make it easy for the rich that he does not have to go out and make the <i>eruv</i> with his feet<sup class="footnote-marker">19</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Eruvin 3:8:3" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Eruvin.3.8.3">Chapter 3, Notes 179–184</a>.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> Paragraph. “Rebbi Simeon says, to what is this similar,” etc. “If somebody was on the road and is afraid lest it get dark,” etc. “If he does not know or is not conversant with practice,” etc. “That is what they said, the poor person makes an <i>eruv</i> with his feet,” etc.<sup class="footnote-marker">82</sup><i class="footnote">The discussion is only about <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Eruvin 4:8:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Eruvin.4.8.1">Mishnah 10</a>.</i> Rebbi Meïr is of the opinion, the main point of an <i>eruv</i> is by a loaf<sup class="footnote-marker">83</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Eruv teḥumim</i> can be made by depositing a meal at the Sabbath border, and this means bread with additions, or by staying at the place like a traveller.</i>. Why did they say, by his feet? To make it easy for the poor who has no loaf. And Rebbi Jehudah said, the main point of an <i>eruv</i> is by his feet. Why did they say, by a loaf? To make it easy for the rich person that he does not have to go out by his feet<sup class="footnote-marker">84</sup><i class="footnote">But he may send his <i>eruv</i> by any member of his household. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Eruvin 52a" href="/Eruvin.52a">Babli 52a</a>.</i>.
Even though Rebbi Jehudah said, the main point of an <i>eruv</i> is by his feet, only that he should not sit in his house and say, my Sabbath rest should be acquired at place x. But he should go out to (the field) [the Sabbath boundary]<sup class="footnote-marker">85</sup><i class="footnote">The text in parentheses is the scribe’s, confirmed by Raviah (p. 457 <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Eruvin 4:1:2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Eruvin.4.1.2">Note 23</a>); the text in brackets is the corrector’s; it seems induced by the statement “my Sabbath rest should be acquired at <i>this place</i>”, which in Raviah (<i>l. c</i>., Note 24) reads “ “my Sabbath rest should be acquired at <i>place x</i>”, which means that R. Jehudah does <i>not</i> require the person to be at the Sabbath boundary but only to leave his house and go in the direction of his destination for the next day, when the rules of a traveller apply to him and he can determine his Sabbath center from a distance.</i> and say, my Sabbath rest should be acquired at this place, and wait there until it gets dark; then return to his village. And it was stated thus<sup class="footnote-marker">86</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Eruvin 51" href="/Eruvin.51">Babli 51 b</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Eruvin (Lieberman) 3:17" href="/Tosefta_Eruvin_(Lieberman).3.17">Tosephta 3:17</a>.</i>: “It happened that the family of Bet Mamma<sup class="footnote-marker">87</sup><i class="footnote">In the Babylonian sources “Mamal”; Raviah: “Dima.”</i> and the family of Bet Gorion in Ruma were distributing dried figs in years of draught, that the poor of Shiḥin were going out, make <i>eruv</i> with their feet, waiting there until nightfall. The next day they were going there, ate there, and returned. And all their actions they were doing on the advice of the Sages.”

Halakhah 9

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> If somebody started to go to another town for which one makes an <i>eruv</i> but another person intercepted him, he is permitted to go but the remainder of the town is forbidden, the words of Rebbi Jehudah. Rebbi Meïr says, anybody who could have made an <i>eruv</i> but did not make the <i>eruv</i> is a donkey driver-camel driver<sup class="footnote-marker">19</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Eruvin 3:8:3" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Eruvin.3.8.3">Chapter 3, Notes 179–184</a>.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> Paragraph. “If somebody started to go to another town.” One may give this two interpretations. If he said, I shall make an <i>eruv</i> for you and your townspeople, and made the <i>eruv</i> for his townspeople but not for him. He is forbidden to go in that direction<sup class="footnote-marker">88</sup><i class="footnote">More than 2’000 cubits.</i> but permitted all other directions in his town; they are permitted to go in that direction but forbidden all other directions in their town<sup class="footnote-marker">89</sup><i class="footnote">Since the entire town is treated as if it were 4 cubits, they are forbidden all directions outside a circle of radius 2’000 centered at the place of the <i>eruv</i>. Making an <i>eruv teḥumim</i> automatically shrinks the permitted space from a square of edge length 4’000 to a circle of diameter 4’000.</i>. One may give it another interpretation. If he said, I shall make an <i>eruv</i> for you and your townspeople and made the <i>eruv</i> neither for his townspeople nor for him. He is permitted to go in that direction for his feet already acquired for him the day before<sup class="footnote-marker">90</sup><i class="footnote">Following the rules of <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Eruvin 4:7:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Eruvin.4.7.1">Mishnah 8</a>.</i>; they are forbidden to go in that direction but permitted all other directions in his town.

Halakhah 10

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> If somebody left the Sabbath domain for even one cubit he may not reenter. Rebbi Simeon says, Rebbi Eleazar says, for two he may re-enter, three he may not re-enter. If somebody was outside the Sabbath domain at nightfall for even one cubit he may not enter. Rebbi Simeon says, even fifteen cubits he may enter since the rope-spanners do not exhaust the measure because of errors<sup class="footnote-marker">20</sup><i class="footnote">This introduces the first topic of the next Chapter, the determination of the Sabbath boundaries of a town. Since the exact determination of a linear distance would require multiple measurements, the officials charged with marking the borders will intentionally err on the side of caution. In case of need one may assume that the official measurement is 0.75% short of the true value.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> Paragraph. “If somebody left the Sabbath domain,” etc. Rebbi Aḥa in the name of Rebbi Ḥinena and Rav Ḥasdai both are saying, he said only “two”. Therefore could he enter with two and a little bit? Since this is Rebbi Eleazar’s, as Rebbi Eleazar said, “for two he may re-enter, three he may not re-enter.” Rebbi Yose told him, one says at the end, “three he may not re-enter,” therefore three minus a little bit he may re-enter<sup class="footnote-marker">91</sup><i class="footnote">The statement of R. Eleazar in Mishnah 12 does not permit to decide what happens if a person left the Sabbath domain for more than two but less than three cubits.</i>. They wanted to say, what Rebbi Eleazar said is about one who left, therefore not about one who stayed overnight<sup class="footnote-marker">92</sup><i class="footnote">Since R. Eleazar speaks only about a person who left his Sabbath domain, not a traveller whose 2’000 (or 4’000) cubits end just two cubits short of the Sabbath domain of the next town. Since practice follows the Sages, these problems do not have to be resolved.</i>. It was found stated, one is like the other. They wanted to say, what Rebbi Simeon said is about one who stayed overnight, therefore not about one who left. It was found stated, one is like the other.

Chapter 5



Halakhah 1

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> How does one complete towns? A house is recessed, a house is protruding, a superstructure<sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">Greek πῆγμα, τό. This expression is used for all structures that are not human dwellings. The <i>pegma</i> of a city wall is a watch tower. The example of the Babylonian Geonim (<i>geonim Harkavi</i> p. 182) is a dove-cote.</i> is recessed, a superstructure is protruding<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">Since the Sabbath domain of a built-up area is a rectangle oriented NS-EW one starts measuring from a line, oriented NS or EW, which touches the built-up area but leaves the area entirely to one side of the line. In mathematical terminology the completion of the town is the area enclosed on a map of the town by its support lines oriented NS and EW.</i>. If there were walls of ruins ten hand-breadths high or bridges or mausoleums containing dwellings<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote">This also refers to bridges.</i> they extend the measure correspondingly and one makes it like a rectangular table, in order to include the corners<sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote">Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Eruvin 4:7:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Eruvin.4.7.1">Chapter 4, Note 18</a>.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> “How does one complete towns,” etc. “A house is recessed,” one moves it out in line with the town; “a superstructure is protruding,” one moves the town out in line with it<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">Since the Sabbath domain of a built-up area is a rectangle oriented NS-EW one starts measuring from a line, oriented NS or EW, which touches the built-up area but leaves the area entirely to one side of the line. In mathematical terminology the completion of the town is the area enclosed on a map of the town by its support lines oriented NS and EW.</i>.
<sup class="footnote-marker">25</sup><i class="footnote">This is a re-arranged and slightly shortened paragraph from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Berakhot 8:6:10" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Berakhot.8.6.10"><i>Berakhot</i> 8:7, Notes 157–158</a>. In the last example, from <i>Avodah zarah</i>, the text in <i>Berakhot</i> attributes the word with ע to Rav and with א to Samuel. This also is required by the text here.</i> Rav says <i>meˋabberin</i>, and Samuel says <i>me′abberin</i>. He who says <i>meˋabberin</i>, one adds a limb (אבר) to it. And he who says <i>me‘abberin</i>, like a pregnant (עוברה) woman. There, we have stated<sup class="footnote-marker">26</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Berakhot 8:6:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Berakhot.8.6.1">Mishnah <i>Berakhot</i> 8:7</a>.</i>: “One does not recite the benediction over a lamp unless one has profited from its light.” Rav says <i>yeˋutu</i>, and Samuel says <i>ye‘utu</i>. He who says <i>ye′utu, but with this we shall be a</i> G<i>reeable to you</i><sup class="footnote-marker">27</sup><i class="footnote">G<i>en</i>. 34:15.</i>. He who says <i>ye‘utu, to know, to inform the weary of wisdom</i><sup class="footnote-marker">28</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Isaiah 50:4" href="/Isaiah.50.4"><i>Is</i>. 50:4</a>.</i>. There we have stated<sup class="footnote-marker">29</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah <i>Avodah zarah</i> 1:1.</i>: “Before the holidays of the Gentiles.” Rav stated <i>ˋedehen</i> and Samuel stated ‘<i>edehen</i>. He who says <i>ˋedehen, for the day of their misfortune</i>(אידם) <i>is near</i><sup class="footnote-marker">30</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 32:35" href="/Deuteronomy.32.35"><i>Deut</i>. 32:35</a>.</i>. He who says ‘<i>edehen, they are their witnesses</i> (עידיהם)<sup class="footnote-marker">21</sup><i class="footnote">Any built-up area in which from one house to the next there are less than 70⅔ cubits, is considered as 4 cubits in this respect.</i>, etc. How does Samuel deal with Rav's reason, <i>they are their witnesses</i>? In the future they will bring to naught their worshippers on the Day of Judgment.
<sup class="footnote-marker">32</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Eruvin 53a" href="/Eruvin.53a">Babli 53a</a>. The entire Yerushalmi text is copied there by R. Ḥananel.</i> Rebbi Joḥanan in the name of Rebbi Hoshaia: one adds a limb to it. <sup class="footnote-marker">33</sup><i class="footnote">The text is parallel to <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Sanhedrin 11:4:4" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Sanhedrin.11.4.4"><i>Sanhedrin</i> 11:6, Notes 68–69</a>.</i> He lifted his eyes and looked at him. He told him, why are you looking at me? Do I need you that you enjoy it? Thirteen years he went and came before his teacher even though he did not need him. Rebbi Samuel in the name of Rebbi Zeˋira: Was it not enough for him to have paid his respects to his teacher since anybody who pays his respects to his teacher is as if he paid his respects to the Divine Presence. Rebbi Berekhiah, Rebbi Jeremiah in the name of Rebbi Ḥiyya bar Abba. It is written<sup class="footnote-marker">34</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 33:7" href="/Exodus.33.7"><i>Ex</i>. 33:7</a>.</i> <i>and Moses would take the Tent</i>, etc. How far away was it? One <i>mil</i><sup class="footnote-marker">35</sup><i class="footnote">2’000 cubits. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Shemot Rabbah 45:4" href="/Shemot_Rabbah.45.4"><i>Ex. rabba</i> 45(4</a>).</i>. It is not written “and it was that anybody asking Moses” but <i>and it was that anybody asking the Eternal</i>. From here that anybody visiting his teacher is as if he was visiting the Divine Presence. Rebbi Ḥelbo, Rebbi<sup class="footnote-marker">36</sup><i class="footnote">Read: Rav.</i> Ḥuna in the name of Rav: It is written<sup class="footnote-marker">37</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="I Kings 17:1" href="/I_Kings.17.1"><i>1K</i>. 17:1</a>. The verse continues: <i>By the</i> <i>Living Eternal</i> … <i>before Whom I stood</i>.</i>, <i>Eliahu from Tisbe said,</i> etc. Was not Eliahu the ruler<sup class="footnote-marker">38</sup><i class="footnote">Greek τύραννος, ὁ (<i>Arukh</i> טרן 3).</i> of the prophets? But it teaches that all the time he was standing before his teacher Aḥiyya from Shilo it was as if he stood before the Divine Presence. Rebbi Ḥelbo in the name of those of the House of Shilo: Even when Eliahu wanted water for his face Elisha would put it on his hands. What is the reason? <i>Here is Elisha ben Shafaṭ</i><sup class="footnote-marker">39</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="II Kings 3:11" href="/II_Kings.3.11"><i>2K</i>. 3:11</a>.</i>, it is not written here “who studied Torah”, but <i>who poured water on Eliahu’s hands</i>. It is written<sup class="footnote-marker">40</sup><i class="footnote"><i>IS</i>. 3:1.</i>: <i>The lad Samuel was serving the Eternal before Eli</i>. Did he not only serve Eli? But this teaches that all service which he rendered before his teacher Eli was as if he rendered if before the Divine Presence. Rebbi Ismael stated<sup class="footnote-marker">41</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 18:12" href="/Exodus.18.12"><i>Ex</i>. 18:12</a>. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 18:1-20:23" href="/Exodus.18.1-20.23"><i>Mekhilta dR. Ismael Yitro Parašah</i> 1 (ed. Horovitz-Rabin p. 196</a>).</i>: <i>And Aaron and all the Elders of Israel came to eat bread with Moses’s father-in-law before god</i>. Did they eat before God? But from here that anyone who receives a friend<sup class="footnote-marker">42</sup><i class="footnote">In <i>editio princeps</i> of <i>Mekhilta:</i> Sages; similarly <a class="refLink" data-ref="Berakhot 64a" href="/Berakhot.64a">Babli <i>Berakhot</i> 64a</a>.</i> is as if he received the Divine Presence.
Rebbi Jacob bar Aḥa, Rebbi Yasa in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan, from where do you augment? From the lintel<sup class="footnote-marker">43</sup><i class="footnote">The basic measurement is from the lintel of the city gate.</i> 2’000 cubits. Rebbi Yose said to Rebbi Yasa bar Aḥa: It seems reasonable only from the superstructure. But in front of the town it is unlimited<sup class="footnote-marker">44</sup><i class="footnote">If the city walls form a rectangle and at the corners the towers extend over the walls, one does not extend the town beyond the towers. But if there are suburban dwellings in front of the walls one extends the definition of “city” to include all of suburbia on condition that between city wall and suburb the distance not be greater than 70⅔ cubits.</i>. He said, this also is my opinion. He said to him, what did you see to say “the superstructure”? Or should we say these in the back of the superstructure<sup class="footnote-marker">45</sup><i class="footnote">It is difficult to make sense of this argument. In the opinion of S. Liebermann it means that one might consider the suburb as the real town and the original town as appendix (“superstructure”) to this. Since the suburb has no walls, the entire problem of where to start measuring disappears; it is clear that one starts from the outermost wall of the outermost house.</i>? Rav Naḥman said, at the end of the country<sup class="footnote-marker">46</sup><i class="footnote">He has no objection against extending the Sabbath domain of a city to contain all the country.</i>. The word of Rebbi Simeon implies this, since “Rebbi Simeon ben Yoḥai said, I can cause that one may walk from Tyre to Sidon<sup class="footnote-marker">47</sup><i class="footnote">A full day’s travel. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Eruvin (Lieberman) 4:11" href="/Tosefta_Eruvin_(Lieberman).4.11">Tosephta 4:11</a>.</i>, from Tiberias to Sepphoris, by caves and by barns<sup class="footnote-marker">48</sup><i class="footnote">Greek πύργος, ὁ.</i>.”
May one add superstructure to superstructure<sup class="footnote-marker">49</sup><i class="footnote">Are structures which are not dwellings counted as if they were dwellings so that they include an additional 70⅔ cubits from which to count the town, possibly repeating the process many times.</i>? The word of Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish implies that one adds superstructure to superstructure, since Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish said, I can cause that Bet Maˋon be in the completion of Tiberias. You consider the stadium as if it were full of houses, and the <i>castra</i><sup class="footnote-marker">50</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Castra, -orum, n.</i> a military camp; this is a dwelling.</i> are within 70 and remainder of the stadium, and Bet Maˋon is within 70 and remainder of the <i>castra</i>. If one considers the superstructure, the mausoleum of Siricon<sup class="footnote-marker">51</sup><i class="footnote">It is not clear what was the additional structure appended to the stadium, which reduces the distance to the mausoleum to 70⅔ cubits. The mausoleum itself was identified by an inscription, cf. S. Liebermann, Tarbiz 3, p.209.</i> is not within 70 and remainder, but if one considers the pottery<sup class="footnote-marker">52</sup><i class="footnote">Even if the mausoleum should have been inhabited, the potter’s shop was not. Since together with the uninhabited appendix to the stadium it is needed to make Bet Maˋon accessible from Tiberias, this proves that uninhabited structures are counted as if they were houses.</i>, the mausoleum of Siricon is within 70 and remainder.
May one add completion to completion<sup class="footnote-marker">53</sup><i class="footnote">After the preceding argument it should be obvious that the answer is positive.</i>? The word of Rebbi Simeon implies that one adds completion to completion, since “Rebbi Simeon ben Yoḥai said, I can cause that one may walk from Tyre to Sidon, from Tiberias to Sepphoris, by caves and by barns.” Here for walking, there for completion<sup class="footnote-marker">54</sup><i class="footnote">It could be that one finds a particular path that may be applied to one special situation. This does not mean that it can be applied to determine the Sabbath domain for everybody. Therefore the statement does not prove anything (but proof is not needed.)</i>.
Rebbi Aḥa said, the Elder Rebbi Ḥiyya and Bar Qappara disagree. One said, this you are saying only about a large city. But for a small town the addition should not be more than the core<sup class="footnote-marker">55</sup><i class="footnote">This is a very restrictive condition. For example, if a town were a square of side lengths 1, the suburbs could extend only to a distance of .212 from the walls. The previous discussion always assumed that one has 2’000 cubits outside any augmentation.</i>. But the other said, whether large or small, 2’000 is sufficient.
Rebbi Phineas said, it happened that a bright<sup class="footnote-marker">56</sup><i class="footnote">Greek εὔθικτος, -ον.</i> student studied completions for three and a half years from his teacher; he went and completed Galilee<sup class="footnote-marker">57</sup><i class="footnote">He found enough barns and isolated farmhouses to make the entire Galilee into one Sabbath domain.</i>. He could not finish to complete the South before the time made it impossible<sup class="footnote-marker">58</sup><i class="footnote">The South is the region around Lydda. “The time made it impossible” means that the political situation changed. Since the preceding paragraphs showed that in the time of R. Simeon ben Laqish the domain of Tiberias was not extended, the time of the student must be the 4<sup>th</sup> Century and the political situation which made the project impossible was that the Empire turned Christian.</i>.
Rebbi Abba, Rav Jehudah in the name of Rav: If a town is built like a bow, if between the ends there is [a distance of] 3’999 [cubits] he walks its entirety and outside it 2’000; 4’000 he only has 2’000 cubits from the place of his <i>eruv</i><sup class="footnote-marker">59</sup><i class="footnote">The town is built as a semi-circle. If the radius of the circle is &lt; 2’000, every point in the semi-disk bounded by the circle and the chord (the diameter) joining its end-points is accessible from the semi-circle. Therefore the chord is the border of the completed town and the Sabbath domain is a semi-disk of radius 4’000 plus a rectangular domain of 4’000×2’000 based on the chord plus two quarter disks of radius 2’000. This would imply that the statement of the Mishnah that a Sabbath domain always is a rectangular domain only applies to cities compactly built in the shape of a polygon, and this not in all cases; cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Eruvin (Lieberman) 4:4" href="/Tosefta_Eruvin_(Lieberman).4.4">Tosephta 4:4</a>.</i>. Rebbi Aḥa said, Rebbi Samuel explained it. If he would put his sandals at one place he could go outside and put them on; and if he would put his sandals at another place he could go outside and put them on. He could come from either side to the outside. From one side it is forbidden, from both sides it is permitted<sup class="footnote-marker">60</sup><i class="footnote">A line segment can be the border of the completion of a town only if all of its points are accessible from the town on the Sabbath. Therefore if the radius of the semi-circle is &gt; 2’000, a point distant almost 2’000 from one side is not accessible from the other and the center is not accessible from anywhere. Therefore the chord cannot be the border of the completion; the Sabbath domain only is the set of all points of distance at most 2’000 from any point of the semi-circle. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Eruvin 55a" href="/Eruvin.55a">Babli 55a</a>.</i>.
Rebbi Abba in the name of Rav Jehudah. If there was a large city and in it a ditch ten [hand-breadths] deep and four wide, one looks where it is full of earth and pebbles. Otherwise one considers it open<sup class="footnote-marker">61</sup><i class="footnote">Translation and explanation are tentative. A ditch 10 deep and 4 wide is a domain by itself. If the ditch runs through the entire town, is nowhere filled or bridged, it splits the town into two separate towns; otherwise it is disregarded.</i>.
Rebbi Abba, Ammi bar Ezechiel<sup class="footnote-marker">62</sup><i class="footnote">The brother of Rav Jehudah.</i> in the name of Rav. If a city is built on the banks of a river, if between it and the river are four hand-breadths one measures from the wall, three one measures from the outer bank of the river<sup class="footnote-marker">63</sup><i class="footnote">The bank far away from the city; the river being considered as part of the city wall.</i> unless the river be [wide] more than 70 and remainder<sup class="footnote-marker">64</sup><i class="footnote">Then the outer bank cannot be considered part of the city and one has to measure the Sabbath domain from the city wall.</i>. Where do we hold? If it descends ten hand-breadths in three [cubits] one measures from the outer bank of the river, if in four [cubits] one measures from the wall<sup class="footnote-marker">65</sup><i class="footnote">If the slope from the wall to the river is steep, it is considered an extension of the wall; otherwise it simply is an empty stretch of land.</i>. So where we hold is between three and four.
Rav said, in a town built of tents, everybody measures from his tent. If there were three huts and three barns one measures from the outer one<sup class="footnote-marker">66</sup><i class="footnote">From the outermost tent. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Eruvin 55b" href="/Eruvin.55b">Babli 55b</a>.</i>. Issy objected, is it not written<sup class="footnote-marker">67</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 23:13" href="/Deuteronomy.23.13"><i>Deut</i>. 23:13</a>.</i>, <i>a sign you should have outside the camp</i>? How could they relieve themselves outside<sup class="footnote-marker">68</sup><i class="footnote">The toilets had to be outside the camp. (Even though the verse is written for a military expedition, the argument refers to the regular camp of the Israelites in the desert.) Since the camp was 12 <i>mil</i> wide (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Eruvin 3:4:5" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Eruvin.3.4.5">Chapter 3, Note 136</a>), how could somebody on one side of the camp go and relieve himself on the other side if he could only go one <i>mil</i> from his tent?</i>? Rebbi Ḥiyya the son of Rebbi Sabbatai asked, how could they go to Moses’s house of study? Moses built them three huts and three barns<sup class="footnote-marker">69</sup><i class="footnote">One would have expected that the Tabernacle certainly would be the equivalent of 3 huts and 3 barns, turning the camp into a formal city.</i>. <sup class="footnote-marker">70</sup><i class="footnote">Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shabbat 7:2:46" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shabbat.7.2.46"><i>Šabbat</i> Chapter 7 Note 399</a>, Chapter 12 Note 12. The quote of the present paragraph in <i>Qondros Aḥaron</i> edited by L. Ginzberg in his <i>Yerushalmi Fragments</i> p. 318 reads here the exact text of <i>Šabbat</i> Chapter 12. Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Eruvin 55b" href="/Eruvin.55b">Babli 55b</a>.</i> Rebbi Yose says, because they were travelling and camping by the Word, was it not temporary? Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun said, since the Holy One, praise to Him, has promised them that he would bring them into the Land, it is as if it were permanent. Because of this<sup class="footnote-marker">71</sup><i class="footnote">That the camp could be considered a permanent city. (<i>Qondros Aḥaron</i> reads “R. Abun”).</i> Rebbi Abbin said, Moses built them three huts and three barns.
“One makes it rectangular in the four directions of the world<sup class="footnote-marker">2,</sup><i class="footnote">Since the Sabbath domain of a built-up area is a rectangle oriented NS-EW one starts measuring from a line, oriented NS or EW, which touches the built-up area but leaves the area entirely to one side of the line. In mathematical terminology the completion of the town is the area enclosed on a map of the town by its support lines oriented NS and EW.</i><sup class="footnote-marker">72</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Eruvin 56a" href="/Eruvin.56a">Babli 56a</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Eruvin (Lieberman) 4:6" href="/Tosefta_Eruvin_(Lieberman).4.6">Tosephta 4:6</a>. R. Yose here is the Tanna, ben Ḥalaphta.</i>, so that its Western direction be in the West of the world and its Southern direction be in the South of the world. Rebbi Yose said, if he does not know how to determine the directions let him go and learn from the solstices. From the place where the sun rises on the day of the summer solstice to the place where it rises on the day of the winter solstice is Eastern direction; from the place where the sun goes down on the day of the winter solstice to the place where it goes down on the day of the summer solstice is Western direction; the remainder are North and South. That is what is written<sup class="footnote-marker">73</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Ecclesiastes 1:6" href="/Ecclesiastes.1.6"><i>Eccl</i>. 1:6</a>.</i>, <i>it goes to the South and turns to the North. It goes to the South</i> during the day <i>and turns to the North</i> during the night; <i>all around in circles goes the wind, to its circuits returns the wind</i>, these are Eastern and Western directions<sup class="footnote-marker">74</sup><i class="footnote">The main directions of the wind.</i>.”
One understands this for Shilo and the Temple<sup class="footnote-marker">75</sup><i class="footnote">They could be exactly built EW-NS; this statement is the introduction to the next paragraph about the orientation of the Tabernacle in the desert.</i>, as Rebbi Aḥa said in the name of Samuel bar Rav Isaac, how much did the earlier prophets exercise themselves to make the Eastern gate so that the sun be exactly on it on the summer solstice and the winter solstice<sup class="footnote-marker">76</sup><i class="footnote">It seems that one should read: the spring and autumn equinoxes, but there is no textual evidence for this.</i>. It was called by seven names: the gate “desist”<sup class="footnote-marker">77</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="II Kings 11:6" href="/II_Kings.11.6"><i>2K</i>. 11:6</a>.</i>, the foundation gate<sup class="footnote-marker">78</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="II Chronicles 23:5" href="/II_Chronicles.23.5"><i>2Chr</i>. 23:5</a>.</i>, the sun gate<sup class="footnote-marker">79</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jeremiah 19:2" href="/Jeremiah.19.2"><i>Jer</i>. 19:2</a>.</i>, the entrance gate<sup class="footnote-marker">80</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezekiel 40:15" href="/Ezekiel.40.15"><i>Ez</i>. 40:15</a>.</i>, the middle gate<sup class="footnote-marker">81</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jeremiah 39:3" href="/Jeremiah.39.3"><i>Jer</i>. 39:3</a>.</i> the new gate<sup class="footnote-marker">82</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jeremiah 26:10" href="/Jeremiah.26.10"><i>Jer</i>. 26:10</a>.</i>, the upper gate<sup class="footnote-marker">83</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="II Chronicles 24:20" href="/II_Chronicles.24.20"><i>2Chr</i>. 24:20</a>.</i>. The gate “desist” since there the impure separate<sup class="footnote-marker">84</sup><i class="footnote">Anybody not pure was barred from the entire Temple Mount, but those who needed a Temple ceremony for purification, such as the healed sufferer from skin disease, did come to the entrance gate of the Temple proper.</i>; that is what is written<sup class="footnote-marker">85</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Lamentations 4:15" href="/Lamentations.4.15"><i>Lament</i>. 4:15</a>.</i>, <i>desist, impure one calls them</i>. The foundation gate, for there practice was founded. The sun gate, since it was directed towards sunrise, as you are saying<sup class="footnote-marker">86</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Job 9:7" href="/Job.9.7"><i>Job</i> 9:7</a>.</i>, <i>Who says to the sun not to shine</i>. The entrance gate, since it serves as entry and exit. The middle gate, since it is fixed between two gates<sup class="footnote-marker">87</sup><i class="footnote">The Temple door and the entrance gate to the Temple Mount.</i>. The new gate, for there the Sopherim renewed practice. The upper gate, since it was higher than the courtyard of Israel and the courtyard of women<sup class="footnote-marker">88</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Yoma 26b" href="/Yoma.26b">R. Ḥananel (<i>ad Yoma</i> 26b</a>, bottom) reads: since it was higher than the courtyard. Probably it means that the Eastern gate was built higher than the wall and the other gates since it was crowned by a tower depicting the fortress of Susa (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Middot 1:3" href="/Mishnah_Middot.1.3">Mishnah <i>Middot</i> 1:3</a>).</i>. The Temple had another distinction<sup class="footnote-marker">89</sup><i class="footnote">In quite a number of items was the Temple distinguished relative to the Tabernacle at Shilo.</i>.
Who was determining them the directions in the desert<sup class="footnote-marker">90</sup><i class="footnote">Since the Tabernacle had to be oriented strictly EW (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 2" href="/Numbers.2"><i>Num</i>. 2</a>). <a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 12" href="/Numbers.12"><i>Tanḥuma Bemidbar</i> (12</a>).</i>? Rebbi Aḥa said, the Ark did determine the directions for them. That is what is written<sup class="footnote-marker">91</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 10:21" href="/Numbers.10.21"><i>Num</i>. 10:21</a>.</i>, <i>then travelled the Kohatites, the carriers of the Sanctuary</i>, this is the Ark. <i>And</i> the Mererites <i>erected the dwelling before they came,</i> the Kohatites on whom the Ark was placed.
<sup class="footnote-marker">92</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 10:25" href="/Numbers.10.25">Rashi <i>Num</i>. 10:25</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 2:17" href="/Numbers.2.17">2:17</a>.</i> How did Israel travel in the desert? Rebbi Ḥama bar Ḥanina and Rebbi Hoshaia<sup class="footnote-marker">93</sup><i class="footnote">In <i>Qondros aḥaron</i>: R. Joshua ben Levi.</i>. One said, like a chest, but the other said, like a beam. He who said like a chest, <i>just as they camped so they travelled</i><sup class="footnote-marker">94</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Num</i>.2:17.</i>. He who said like a beam, <i>the collector of all camps with their armies</i><sup class="footnote-marker">95</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 10:25" href="/Numbers.10.25"><i>Num</i>. 10:25</a>.</i>. How does he who said like a beam explain him who said like a chest, <i>just as they camped so they travelled</i>? Just as they camped following the Word, so they travelled following the Word. How does he who said like a chest explain him who said like a beam, <i>the collector of all camps with their armies</i>? Since the tribe of Dan was so populous<sup class="footnote-marker">95a</sup><i class="footnote">Greek ὄχλος, ὁ, “multitude”.</i> it travelled last and to anybody who had lost anything they would return it to him; that is what is written, <i>the collector of all camps with their armies</i>.
It was stated in the name of Rebbi Jehudah: “Also its ledges and walls were measured with it.<sup class="footnote-marker">96</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Eruvin (Lieberman) 4:7" href="/Tosefta_Eruvin_(Lieberman).4.7">Tosephta 4:7</a>. One starts measuring not from the wall of the city or the last house but from the first place which is under the open sky.</i>” Rav Hoshaia asked: is the airspace of a courtyard measured with it<sup class="footnote-marker">97</sup><i class="footnote">If the town is completed by adding suburban buildings, are only houses added or any enclosed space?</i>? Let us hear from the following: A house which was breached on one side is measured with it, from two sides it is not measured with it. Rebbi Abbin in the name of Rav Jehudah, if its beam<sup class="footnote-marker">98</sup><i class="footnote">The house is considered breached only if the ceiling beams also are missing.</i> had been removed. But if its beam had not been removed it is measured with it. If the beam had been removed is it not like the airspace of a courtyard? There it was enclosed as a dwelling, here it was not enclosed as a dwelling.<sup class="footnote-marker">99</sup><i class="footnote">Therefore only dwelling space is added as completion.</i> “If he measures he should not be measuring from the center since he would lose, but from the corners.<sup class="footnote-marker">100</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Eruvin (Lieberman) 4:13" href="/Tosefta_Eruvin_(Lieberman).4.13">Tosephta 4:13</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Eruvin 56b" href="/Eruvin.56b">Babli 56b</a>. Since one determines a Sabbath boundary as a straight line running either NS or EW it really does not matter where one starts measuring. The Tosephta states that one should not consider the starting point of the measuring as center of a circle but as a corner. The Sabbath domain always is a rectangular domain.</i>”

Halakhah 2

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> One gives a fore-court to the city<sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote">One does not start to measure the 2’000 cubits outside the town from the wall of the (easternmost, northernmost, etc.) house but only at a distance of √5000 ~ 70⅔ cubits (cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Eruvin 2:5:2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Eruvin.2.5.2">Chapter 2, Note 82</a>).</i>, the words of Rebbi Meïr; but the Sages say that a fore-court was mentioned only between two villages, if each of them has seventy cubits and a remainder, the fore-courts of both make it one. Similarly three villages forming a triangle, if between the two outer ones there are 141⅓ [cubits], the middle one makes all three to be one<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">If the three towns form a triangle and the (necessarily parallel, either NS or EW) lines of support of two pairs of towns are no more than 2×70⅔ = 141⅓ cubits apart, the entire complex is considered one town and without an <i>eruv</i> each inhabitant may walk through all of them and outside 2’000 cubits measured from the outermost lines.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> Paragraph. “One gives a fore-court to the city<sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote">One does not start to measure the 2’000 cubits outside the town from the wall of the (easternmost, northernmost, etc.) house but only at a distance of √5000 ~ 70⅔ cubits (cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Eruvin 2:5:2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Eruvin.2.5.2">Chapter 2, Note 82</a>).</i>,” etc. Rav Ḥuna in the name of [Rav]<sup class="footnote-marker">101</sup><i class="footnote">Missing in L, inserted from the quote of the text by Rashba, col. 334. Rav Huna is not known to have had any teacher but Rav.</i>: Rebbi Meïr and the rabbis explain the same verse. Rebbi Meïr explained: <i>From the city wall</i>, why does the verse say, <i>outwards</i><sup class="footnote-marker">102</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 35:4" href="/Numbers.35.4"><i>Num</i>. 35:4</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Eruvin 57a" href="/Eruvin.57a">Babli 57a</a>. He reads the verse that one does not start measuring from the city wall but somewhere outside. The definition of “outside” is given over to the rabbinic authorities.</i>? From here that one gives a fore-court to the city. The rabbis explained, <i>outwards,</i> why does the verse say, <i>from the city wall</i>? From that one does (not)<sup class="footnote-marker">103</sup><i class="footnote">This was written by the scribe but (wrongly) deleted by the corrector who then (wrongly) inserted the relative pronoun in the following space.</i> give a fore-court to the city<sup class="footnote-marker">104</sup><i class="footnote">They read the word as stating that one measures outward at a right angle to the wall, starting from the wall.</i>. Does this not mean that one gives a fore-court to the city<sup class="footnote-marker">105</sup><i class="footnote">This refers to the second part of <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Eruvin 5:2:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Eruvin.5.2.1">Mishnah 2</a>, where it is stated that two villages less than 141⅓ cubits apart are considered a single village for the rules of the Sabbath. This statement seems incompatible with the reading of the verse attributed to the rabbis.</i>? Rebbi Jacob bar Aḥa, Rebbi Abuna, Rebbi Naḥum in the name of Rebbi Samuel bar Abba, the Mishnah is finished<sup class="footnote-marker">105</sup><i class="footnote">This refers to the second part of <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Eruvin 5:2:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Eruvin.5.2.1">Mishnah 2</a>, where it is stated that two villages less than 141⅓ cubits apart are considered a single village for the rules of the Sabbath. This statement seems incompatible with the reading of the verse attributed to the rabbis.</i>.
Paragraph<sup class="footnote-marker">107</sup><i class="footnote">Continuation of the discussion of <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Eruvin 5:2:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Eruvin.5.2.1">Mishnah 2</a>.</i>. “Similarly three villages forming a triangle,” etc. Samuel said, if they are in a line<sup class="footnote-marker">108</sup><i class="footnote">The three villages are more or less in one line; meaning that if one walks from one of the outer ones to the other outer one by necessity one crosses the territory of the middle one.</i>. Bar Qappara said, it they are like a tripod<sup class="footnote-marker">109</sup><i class="footnote">An acute triangle.</i>. Which one is the middle one? It is understandable for him who said, they are in a line. For him who said, they are like a tripod, which one is the middle one? Rebbi Samuel, Rebbi Berekhiah’s brother, said, if you are measuring from one, the other is the middle one; if you are measuring from one, the other is the middle one<sup class="footnote-marker">110</sup><i class="footnote">In an acute triangle every edge can be chosen as basis; the remaining vertex then is between the other two.</i>. Rebbi Jacob bar Aḥa, Rebbi Yasa in the name of Rebbi Ḥanina, only if the middle one not be farther than 2’000 cubits<sup class="footnote-marker">111</sup><i class="footnote">The problem becomes acute only if one of the angles of the triangle is very small compared to the other two; then the vertex with the small angle is in between the other two. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Eruvin 57b" href="/Eruvin.57b">Babli 57b</a>.</i>. Rebbi Yose said, I objected before Rebbi Jocob bar Aḥa, did we not state: “if between the two outer ones are 141⅓ [cubits], the middle one makes all three [to be one]<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">If the three towns form a triangle and the (necessarily parallel, either NS or EW) lines of support of two pairs of towns are no more than 2×70⅔ = 141⅓ cubits apart, the entire complex is considered one town and without an <i>eruv</i> each inhabitant may walk through all of them and outside 2’000 cubits measured from the outermost lines.</i>.” To permit the two outer ones<sup class="footnote-marker">112</sup><i class="footnote">If the distance between villages A,B is &lt; 141⅓ and AC, BC are large but &lt; 2’000 then since one may walk from A to C and from B to C one may make of A and B one village by <i>eruv</i> but not A and C nor B and C.</i>. If there were two, could the middle one be counted for either side? His problem was if there were two people walking. But if one person is walking, it is counted for either side<sup class="footnote-marker">113</sup><i class="footnote">If there are 3 villages forming a triangle there is no problem. But if there are 5, A<sub>1</sub> A<sub>2</sub> B<sub>1</sub> B<sub>2</sub> C, and C is an acceptable third both for A<sub>1</sub>B<sub>1</sub> and A<sub>2</sub>B<sub>2</sub>, there is a problem if two people are walking simultaneously from A<sub>i</sub> to B<sub>i</sub> (i=1,2) since it is not determined for which triangle C should be counted. But if only one person walks, since <i>eruvim</i> are rabbinic we may say that retroactively it became clear that C belongs to where it is needed.</i>.

Halakhah 3

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> One only measures with a rope of 50 cubits, neither less nor more. One should only measure holding up to his heart<sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote">The measure should be made strictly horizontal. The two people holding the measuring tape hold it on their breasts, far from the ground, to hold it as exactly horizontal as possible.</i>. If he was measuring and came to a valley or a wall he circumvents it and returns to his measurement, on condition that he not exit the Sabbath domain<sup class="footnote-marker">8</sup><i class="footnote">If one measures, e. g., N to S, and comes to an obstacle, one should go exactly E or W until the obstacle disappears, resume measuring due S, and then return on an exactly EW path to the original line and resume measuring.</i>. If he cannot circumvent it, about this said Rebbi Dositheos ben Yannai in the name of Rebbi Meïr: I heard that one strip-measures<sup class="footnote-marker">9</sup><i class="footnote">One measures with a short rope of 4 cubits held horizontally.</i> in the mountains<sup class="footnote-marker">10</sup><i class="footnote">As explained in the Halakhah, one measures with a rope of 4 cubits which can be held horizontal also on steep inclines. The 2’000 cubits which one determines are not actual distances but the length of the projection of a path onto the plane locally representing the surface of a flat Earth.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> Paragraph. “One only measures with a rope of 50 cubits,” etc. How much is the measure of the Sabbath domain? 40 ropes. “Neither less” since it can be tightened and increases, “nor more” since it gets loose and loses<sup class="footnote-marker">116</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Eruvin 58" href="/Eruvin.58">Babli 58</a> a.</i>. Some Tannaim state, one measures with a linen rope, but some Tannaim state, with a chain rope<sup class="footnote-marker">117</sup><i class="footnote">A metal chain.</i>, and some Tannaim state, with a rope of four cubits. <sup class="footnote-marker">116</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Eruvin 58" href="/Eruvin.58">Babli 58</a> a.</i> Rebbi Joshua said, there is no truer measure than with chains, but what can I do since in Prophets it is written ropes, <i>a linen twine was in his hand and a measuring rod</i><sup class="footnote-marker">118</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezekiel 40:3" href="/Ezekiel.40.3"><i>Ez</i>. 40:3</a>.</i>.
If from him to a river were 75 cubits. Two Amoraim, one said, he measures with a rope of 50 cubits and returns 25 cubits; but the other one said, he measures with a rope of 50 cubits and the remainder he measures with a rope of four cubits. If the river was narrow on top and wide below, up to 50 cubits one considers it as if full of dust and pebbles; otherwise one sees it inclining upwards and inclining downwards<sup class="footnote-marker">119</sup><i class="footnote">If a canyon is up to 50 cubits wide on top one simply measures on top and disregards what is below; otherwise one has to measure the slopes.</i>. If the river was bent, Rebbi Ḥasdai says, with telescopes he estimates in the plain and does the same with a mountain<sup class="footnote-marker">120</sup><i class="footnote">If one has a secure base of given length it is more accurate anyhow to determine lengths by measuring angles with a theodolite.</i>. Rebbi Aḥa, Rebbi Ḥinena, Rebbi Jeremiah in the name of Rebbi Samuel bar Rav Isaac: only if the measure results in the mountain four hand-breadths as a place<sup class="footnote-marker">121</sup><i class="footnote">In mountainous terrain one measures with ropes of 4 cubits length. It is considered an incline which needs special treatment only if the difference in height for the length of the rope is 4 hand-breadths, ⅔ of a cubit. Let α be the angle of inclination, this means sin α = .167 or α = 4.5°. Since cos α = .958, the error committed by measuring the slope instead of its horizontal projection is 1.42%.</i>. Rebbi Yose, Rebbi Abuna in the name of Rav Jehudah, Rebbi Yudan has it in the name of Rav: If one holds it high above his head and the other by his feet, everybody agrees that one strip-measures<sup class="footnote-marker">122</sup><i class="footnote">While the Sages state in the Mishnah that one does not strip-measure at mountains, i. e., that one measures the distance on the ground, not the horizontal projection, they agree that if the slope is very steep the error would be too large and one must work with projections. To translate the rules given here into numbers would require exact data about the length of a cubit and the average height of a man; these are not available. For a rough estimate one may assume that the average height of a man be 3.5 cubits. Then if in a team of geometers one holds his end of the rope of 4 cubits on top of his head while the other, climbing up the mountain, has to hold his end at his feet in order to keep the rope horizontal, the slope is given by tan α = 3.5/4 = 0.875 or α = 41<sup class="footnote-marker">°</sup>11’. In this case the distance measured on the slope would be 5⅓ cubits; measuring on the slope instead of with an horizontal rope would decrease the Sabbath distance by more than a third. In this case the Sages have to agree with R. Meïr.</i>. The high one over his head and the low one on his hips, everybody agrees that one strip-measures<sup class="footnote-marker">123</sup><i class="footnote">Probably that means tan α = .25, α ~14°, the error in measurement is ~ 5%.</i>. Where do they disagree? On his heart; Rebbi Meïr says one strip-measures but the Sages say one does not strip-measure<sup class="footnote-marker">124</sup><i class="footnote">If the difference is only half a cubit, tan α = .125, α ~ 7°; the error in measurement is ~ 1.2%, which is not worth the bother; the position of the Sages is justified.</i>.
<sup class="footnote-marker">125</sup><i class="footnote">This text is from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Sotah 5:3:2-4" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Sotah.5.3.2-4"><i>Soṭah</i> 5:5</a>, explained in detail in Notes 120–123 and <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Makkot 2:7:3-4" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Makkot.2.7.3-4"><i>Makkot</i> 2:7 (Notes 141–142</a>).</i> Rebbi Abba in the name of Rebbi Jehudah, Rebbi Zeˋira in the name of Mar Uqba: One strip-measures only with a rope of 50 cubits. Rebbi Zeˋira in the name of Rav Ḥasdai: One strip-measures (only in mountains but)<sup class="footnote-marker">126</sup><i class="footnote">With the other two sources read: :Not for Levitic cities.</i> not for the place of breaking the calf’s neck. This would be acceptable for him who says, 1000 cubits of open space and 2000 cubits of Sabbath domain. But for him who says, 1000 cubits of open space and 2000 cubits of fields and vineyards, did they not learn the Sabbath domain from the Levitic cities? For the main thing one does not strip-measure; does one strip-measure for the derivative?
<sup class="footnote-marker">127</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 35:3" href="/Numbers.35.3"><i>Num</i>. 35:3</a>.</i> From where that one does not bury in Levitic cities? Rebbi Abbahu in the name of Rebbi Yose bar Ḥanina: <i>And their open spaces shall be for their animals</i> … <i>and all their lives</i><sup class="footnote-marker">128</sup><i class="footnote">This paragraph is copied here only as an appendix to the preceding; it does not belong here.</i>. They were given for living; they were not given for burials.

Halakhah 4

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> Surveys may only be made by professionals. If one extended the place and restricted it at another, one listens to him who extends<sup class="footnote-marker">11</sup><i class="footnote">If the town has a traditional Sabbath boundary and a professional geometer tells them that at a certain place the actual boundary is farther away, one listens to the expert. The Yerushalmi does not express an opinion about what to do if the experts determine that the original border is too far away.</i>. Even a slave or a slave woman are trustworthy to say up to here is the Sabbath domain since the Sages said in these matters not to restrict but to be lenient<sup class="footnote-marker">12</sup><i class="footnote">Since Sabbath boundaries are rabbinic institutions only.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> Paragraph. “Surveys may only be made by professionals,” etc. One does not listen to a non-professional who added<sup class="footnote-marker">129</sup><i class="footnote">Greek ἰδιώτης, ὁ. A non-professional may testify to the limits of the traditional Sabbath domain (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Eruvin (Lieberman) 4:16" href="/Tosefta_Eruvin_(Lieberman).4.16">Tosephta 4:16</a>, see below) but may not initiate any changes. Rashba col. 345.</i>.
<sup class="footnote-marker">130</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Eruvin 3:4:5" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Eruvin.3.4.5">Chapter 3, Notes 134–136</a>.</i> Rebbi Hoshaia said: You must conclude that the boundaries of Sabbath domains are not clear in the words of the Torah. Rebbi Mana asked, it is accepted that 2’000 cubits is not clear. Are 4’000 cubits not clear? Rebbi Simeon bar Carsana in the name of Rebbi Aḥa: The only clear case among all of them is the domain of twelve <i>mil</i> of the camp of Israel.

Halakhah 5

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> A village which is the property of one person<sup class="footnote-marker">13</sup><i class="footnote">And therefore is considered one dwelling where one may carry in the entire place without an <i>eruv</i>. If it turns into a place with multiple owners, an <i>eruv</i> is needed.</i> and becomes owned by many can have one <i>eruv</i> in its entirety; but for one of multiple ownership<sup class="footnote-marker">14</sup><i class="footnote">Where one needs an <i>eruv</i> to make it possible to carry in the alleys. If now an individual buys up all property in the village it should not be forgotten that the place originally needed an <i>eruv</i>; therefore some part should be left outside the main compound in which one may carry freely.</i> which became one of single ownership one does not make an <i>eruv</i> in its entirety unless one leaves outside [a part] like the town Ḥadašah in Jehudah<sup class="footnote-marker">15</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Joshua 15:37" href="/Joshua.15.37"><i>Jos</i>. 15:37</a>.</i> which has 50 inhabitants<sup class="footnote-marker">16</sup><i class="footnote">Including children and women.</i>, the words of Rebbi Jehudah. Rebbi Simeon says, three courtyards of two houses each.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> Paragraph: “A village which is the property of one person<sup class="footnote-marker">13</sup><i class="footnote">And therefore is considered one dwelling where one may carry in the entire place without an <i>eruv</i>. If it turns into a place with multiple owners, an <i>eruv</i> is needed.</i> and becomes owned by many,” etc. It was stated in the name of Rebbi Jehudah: One does not make an <i>eruv</i> in parts. Rebbi Jehudah’s argument is inverted since Rebbi Ḥiyya stated:<sup class="footnote-marker">131</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Eruvin 1:1:23" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Eruvin.1.1.23">Chapter 1, Note 147</a>.</i> How does one permit public domain? Rebbi Jehudah says, a lath on each side or a beam on each side, but the Sages say, a lath and a beam on one side and he makes a door frame on the other side. And here he says so? It was not said about this but about the following: Even a big city like Antioch, if it has a single gate one may make an <i>eruv</i><sup class="footnote-marker">132</sup><i class="footnote">There is only one entrance; no traffic artery crossing the town. Then one <i>eruv</i> can be made for the entire city but no partial one. R. Jehudah states that either one makes no <i>eruv</i> at all or one makes one for the entire city. If one made two <i>eruvim</i> for two different parts of the city both would be invalid. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Eruvin 59" href="/Eruvin.59">Babli 59a/b</a>.</i>. It was stated in the name of Rebbi Jehudah: One does not make an <i>eruv</i> in parts. Rebbi Yose said, this<sup class="footnote-marker">133</sup><i class="footnote">Since the alley has only one exit it is similar to the city with only one gate. If one made two <i>eruvim</i> for two different parts of the alley both would be invalid.</i> implies that if people in an alley put a beam (in) [at the entrance]<sup class="footnote-marker">134</sup><i class="footnote">The text in parentheses is the original text of the scribe, the one in brackets the corrector’s. The corrector’s text is impossible. Medieval quotes of the passage (Rashba col. 351, Ritba <i>ad</i> 59b p. 50d, Meïri <i>ad</i> 59a p. 227a, Rosh Chapter 5 No. 9) all read “in the middle”, and this is the meaning of the scribe’s text. The dwellers in the back part of the dead-end alley put their cross beam not at the entrance of the alley but in the middle. If the dwellers of the outer part do not make their own <i>eruv</i>, the back part <i>eruv</i> is valid. If both parts make their own <i>eruv,</i> neither of them is valid.</i> of the alley then these are permitted and those are prohibited. If both of them put it up, both are prohibited. What does he do? He puts the beam at the entrance of the alley and permits the alley<sup class="footnote-marker">135</sup><i class="footnote">A single common <i>eruv</i>.</i>. If five alleys opened into one alley and they put their beam in the middle of the alley then these are permitted and those are prohibited<sup class="footnote-marker">136</sup><i class="footnote">A beam at the entrance of a separate alley makes possible an <i>eruv</i> for that alley.</i>. If both of them put it up, both are prohibited. What does he do? He puts the beam at the entrance of the alley and permits the alley. Rebbi Phineas immigrated here. He looked at the entrance of the market of the shearers and said to them, did you split your <i>eruv</i>? Rebbi Jehudah bar Shalom told him, it was made to reinforce the houses<sup class="footnote-marker">137</sup><i class="footnote">The beam was there for structural reasons; it was not intended for an <i>eruv</i>.</i>.
“Unless one leaves outside like the town Ḥadašah in Jehudah.” As <i>Senan, Ḥadašah, and Migdal-Gad</i><sup class="footnote-marker">138</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Joshua 15:37" href="/Joshua.15.37"><i>Jos</i>. 15:37</a>.</i>. “Which has 5<sup class="footnote-marker">139</sup><i class="footnote">With the Mishnah read: 50.</i> inhabitants,” even men, women, and children. Assi said, but only Israel. Rebbi Abba bar Mamal, Simeon bar Ḥiyya in the name of Rav: If they open into it<sup class="footnote-marker">140</sup><i class="footnote">The houses which are left out of the <i>eruv</i> have to be accessible from the town, otherwise they could not be part of the <i>eruv</i> and leaving them out would not be reserving anything.</i>. Rebbi Mana said, since they open into it they all are made one domain<sup class="footnote-marker">141</sup><i class="footnote">If houses belong naturally to the town there is no reason to leave them out of the <i>eruv</i>. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Eruvin 60a" href="/Eruvin.60a">Babli 60a</a>.</i>.

Halakhah 6

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> If somebody was in the East and told his son to make him an <i>eruv</i> in the West, or in the West and told his son to make him an <i>eruv</i> in the East, if there are from his place to his house 2’000 cubits but to his <i>eruv</i> more than this, he is permitted up to his house but forbidden to his <i>eruv</i><sup class="footnote-marker">17</sup><i class="footnote">This refers only to somebody who tells his son shortly before sundown on Friday to make an <i>eruv</i> for him, but he goes in the opposite direction and therefore could not reach the place of his <i>eruv</i> before sundown. Then the <i>eruv</i> is invalid for him, but since he ordered an <i>eruv</i> made he lost the rectangular domain of the town dwellers and now can only move in a circle of radius 2’000 cubits.</i>; if to his <i>eruv</i> 2’000 cubits but to his house more than that, he is permitted up to his <i>eruv</i> but forbidden to his house. If somebody puts his <i>eruv</i> in the complement of the town<sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">Greek πῆγμα, τό. This expression is used for all structures that are not human dwellings. The <i>pegma</i> of a city wall is a watch tower. The example of the Babylonian Geonim (<i>geonim Harkavi</i> p. 182) is a dove-cote.</i> he did not do anything<sup class="footnote-marker">18</sup><i class="footnote">Since this is considered part of the town anyhow.</i>. If he puts it outside the domain<sup class="footnote-marker">19</sup><i class="footnote">Not outside the Sabbath domain, since then he could not move outside of 4 cubits, but in the Sabbath domain outside the augmented town. Because he made an <i>eruv</i>, his Sabbath domain is a circle of radius 2’000 centered at the <i>eruv;</i> he loses not only the distances in the direction opposite to that of his <i>eruv</i> but also the rectangular shape of his domain.</i> what he had gained he loses.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> Paragraph. “If somebody was in the East,” etc. Because of the difficulty did Bar Qappara ask, the East of his son and the West of his son? One understands “if there are from his place to his house 2’000 cubits but to his <i>eruv</i> more than this, he is permitted up to his house but forbidden to his <i>eruv</i><sup class="footnote-marker">17</sup><i class="footnote">This refers only to somebody who tells his son shortly before sundown on Friday to make an <i>eruv</i> for him, but he goes in the opposite direction and therefore could not reach the place of his <i>eruv</i> before sundown. Then the <i>eruv</i> is invalid for him, but since he ordered an <i>eruv</i> made he lost the rectangular domain of the town dwellers and now can only move in a circle of radius 2’000 cubits.</i>.” “If to his <i>eruv</i> be 2’000 cubits but to his house more than that, he is permitted up to his <i>eruv</i> but forbidden to his house”<sup class="footnote-marker">142</sup><i class="footnote">If one read the Mishnah as him being in one side of the town and his son in the other side it would be impossible for his house to be farther away than his <i>eruv</i>. Therefore one has to read the Mishnah as “him to the East of his son and the West of his son”. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Eruvin 60b" href="/Eruvin.60b">Babli 60b</a>.</i>?

Halakhah 7

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> The people of a large town walk through all of a small town; the people of a small town walk through all of a large town<sup class="footnote-marker">20</sup><i class="footnote">The text of this Mishnah will be emended in the Halakhah.</i>. How is that? If somebody lived in a large town and put his <i>eruv</i> in a small town, or in a small town and put his <i>eruv</i> in a large town, he walks through all of it<sup class="footnote-marker">21</sup><i class="footnote">Any built-up area in which from one house to the next there are less than 70⅔ cubits, is considered as 4 cubits in this respect.</i> and outside of it 2’000 cubits. But Rebbi Aqiba says, he only has 2’000 cubits from the place of his <i>eruv</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> Paragraph. “The people of a large town walk through all of a small town,” etc. So is the Mishnah: “The people of a large town walk through all of a small town, the people of a small town do not walk through all of a large town<sup class="footnote-marker">143</sup><i class="footnote">The Sabbath domain of the large city is measured from the completion; any village inside the domain is counted only as 4 cubits. If the Sabbath domain of the village reaches only the completion of the city but not the city itself, the city is not counted as 4 cubits for them.</i>. How is that?” There is no “how is that”<sup class="footnote-marker">144</sup><i class="footnote">The next part of the Mishnah is a new sentence, independent of the preceding text.</i>.
Is a city counted in the measure of 2’000<sup class="footnote-marker">145</sup><i class="footnote">If that Sabbath domain of one town reaches another town, is the other town wholly incorporated in the Sabbath domain of the first or not?</i>? Rebbi Ḥizqiah said, Rebbi Simon in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan: A city is not counted in the measure of 2’000. Rebbi Eleazar said, a city is counted in the measure of 2’000<sup class="footnote-marker">146</sup><i class="footnote">For him a city is counted as 4 cubits only if he dwells there, not if it is in the Sabbath domain.</i>. In earlier times the people of Tiberias were walking through all its hot springs but the people of its hot springs came only to the cupola. But today for the people of Tiberias and the people of its hot springs it is one city<sup class="footnote-marker">147</sup><i class="footnote">Enough houses have been built in between to make the hot springs part of the completion of Tiberias.</i>. Rebbi Jeremiah said, <sup class="footnote-marker">148</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Eruvin (Lieberman) 4:16" href="/Tosefta_Eruvin_(Lieberman).4.16">Tosephta 4:16</a>. The Tosephta conflates the stories about Magdala and Gadara.</i>“it happened that an old shepherd came and said before Rebbi, I remember the people of Magdala walking up to its<sup class="footnote-marker">149</sup><i class="footnote">Since the hot springs of Tiberias are near the shores of Lake Genezareth, these must be different hot springs.</i> hot springs, walking through its hot springs and coming up to the outer courtyard close to the bridge; and Rebbi permitted that the people of Magdala walk up to its hot springs, walking through its hot springs and come up to the outer courtyard up to the bridge. <sup class="footnote-marker">150</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Eruvin 61a" href="/Eruvin.61a">Babli 61a</a>.</i> In addition, Rebbi permitted that the people of Gadara descend to their hot springs and return to Gadara but the people of the hot springs may not ascend to Gadara.” Rebbi Mana said, because of the authorities<sup class="footnote-marker">151</sup><i class="footnote">The citizens of Gadara are the masters of Ḥammat Gader and go there without permission; the people of Ḥammat Gader may go to Gadara only with permission.</i>. Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun said, it is not because of this but because we have stated “the people of a large town walk through all of a small town, the people of a small town do not walk through all of a large town<sup class="footnote-marker">143</sup><i class="footnote">The Sabbath domain of the large city is measured from the completion; any village inside the domain is counted only as 4 cubits. If the Sabbath domain of the village reaches only the completion of the city but not the city itself, the city is not counted as 4 cubits for them.</i>.”
